<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ca547623-68cf-464c-b801-d1e481ee4bb3'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer12416459223434041114">After a brutal nuclear war, the United States was left decimated. A small group of survivors eventually banded together, but only after more conflict over which family would govern the new nation. The Westfalls lost. Fifty years later, peace and control are maintained by marrying the daughters of the losing side to the sons of the winning group in a yearly ritual. <br/><br/>This yea</span>
  <span id="freeText12416459223434041114" style="display:none">After a brutal nuclear war, the United States was left decimated. A small group of survivors eventually banded together, but only after more conflict over which family would govern the new nation. The Westfalls lost. Fifty years later, peace and control are maintained by marrying the daughters of the losing side to the sons of the winning group in a yearly ritual. <br /><br />This year, it is my turn. <br /><br />My name is Ivy Westfall, and my mission is simple: to kill the president’s son—my soon-to-be husband—and restore the Westfall family to power. <br /><br />But Bishop Lattimer is either a very skilled actor or he’s not the cruel, heartless boy my family warned me to expect. He might even be the one person in this world who truly understands me. But there is no escape from my fate. I am the only one who can restore the Westfall legacy.<br /><br />Because Bishop <i>must</i> die. And I must be the one to kill him…</span>

<div id="review_1150381279" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1150381279" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1150381279?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=war-setting">war-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1150381279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18091533370612596446"><strong>
  <em>My name is Ivy Westfall, and my mission is simple: to kill the president’s son—my soon-to-be husband—and return the Westfall family to power.</em>
</strong><br/><br/>So the premise is grandiose. <strong>AMAZING.</strong> I didn’t want to expect much from this book, but how could I not, with that enticing blurb and beautiful cover? In fact, it all screamed <strong>KICKASS</strong>! And a kickass dystopian book is always welcome. Always. But this book barely contained any action. There was secrecy and plotting, of course, but no real and convincing ex</span>
  <span id="freeText18091533370612596446" style="display:none"><strong>
  <em>My name is Ivy Westfall, and my mission is simple: to kill the president’s son—my soon-to-be husband—and return the Westfall family to power.</em>
</strong><br /><br />So the premise is grandiose. <strong>AMAZING.</strong> I didn’t want to expect much from this book, but how could I not, with that enticing blurb and beautiful cover? In fact, it all screamed <strong>KICKASS</strong>! And a kickass dystopian book is always welcome. Always. But this book barely contained any action. There was secrecy and plotting, of course, but no real and convincing execution around them.<br /><br />In fact, if I were the main character, not only would I have been<strong> DEAD</strong>, but also very very <strong>BORED</strong>. Ivy doesn’t have a choice; she must marry Bishop, the president’s son. In her post-apocalyptic world, every sixteen/seventeen-year-old boy and girl must take a spouse to procreate. And, if that doesn’t work out, they have one thing left: work. If they don’t follow the rules, they are excommunicated and not-so-gently pushed on the other side of the fence.<br /><br />And those people generally die.<br /><br />But Ivy and her family want everything to change. By killing Bishop and the president, her own father will be able to gain power and integrate democracy to their ‘nation.’ It’s a really good plan and, had it been put to execution with more seriousness and fatality, it could have been a grand success.<br /><br />But then there’s Bishop, the sweet, thoughtful and enigmatic Bishop, who (inconveniently) stole Ivy’s heart. Now the plan…she has doubts. Is it the right thing to do? Does he deserve it? She kept asking those questions <em>
  <strong>ALL PLOT LONG</strong>
</em>. And the thing is, I knew from when they first arrived in their house and Bishop showed himself to be kind to her that everything has been jeopardized already. Ivy was never a criminal, and I didn’t want her to be one, but some action would have been very welcome in the plot.<br /><br />I honestly tried to enjoy this, but Ivy and Bishop’s relationship was so so <strong>TAME</strong>. And predictable. Unsurprising. Sleep-worthy. I saw no chemistry between them, let alone feel any captivating atmosphere throughout the read. Another thing that I didn’t enjoy was the pacing: it was slower than in any dystopian book I have read before, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18710190.Allegiant__Divergent___3_" title="Allegiant (Divergent, #3) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Allegiant</a> aside – not sure if any book could ever beat this latter. Probably because not much is happening. The writing was okay, but very standard when I believe it could have been richer in term of vocabulary.<br /><br />Ivy was sincerely annoying. Overall okay, as a person, but her personality bent toward recklessness oh so many times: <strong><em>Keep your mouth closed, I tell myself. Just shut up. But I can’t […]</em> </strong>and <strong><em>My head knows what a terrible idea this is, screaming me to stop, that’ I’m taking things to far, but […]</em> </strong>and <em>
  <strong>Against my better judgement […]</strong>
</em><br /><br />No! If your instinct tells you to<strong> NOT</strong> do something, then perhaps the wisest thing to do would be listening to it. For once. Needless to say, she was repeatedly busted. She also must have gotten some special treatment because, if I look at the world she lives in, many would have been suspicious toward her and investigated more in her personage to finally put to pieces …everything and resolve the puzzle.<br /><br />I tried to but didn’t agree with her at many points. For instance, she said: <strong>
  <em>Sometimes pain is the only language certain people understand.</em>
</strong> I don’t believe that. I don’t believe you ought to hurt some to make them listen to you but, hey, it’s personal plus very controversial. As this is: <strong>
  <em>I don’t want to give up like my own mother.</em>
</strong> Now, is it because someone commits suicide that they ‘give up’? Not sure, but I certainly didn’t like how easily and with no second thoughts she uttered those words.<br /><br />There barely was any world-building. The setting did vary but they weren’t described enough and absolutely not exploited. The author’s main idea was a good one and quite interesting but her not developing it at its full potential backfired, because I couldn’t believe and imagine this story at one hundred percent in my mind.<br /><br />For those who want a <strong>QUITE</strong> simple and uneventful dystopian read, mostly focused on the characters and the romance (filled with angst), this could probably work for you. I wanted more, though. It could have been so much more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18091533370612596446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16651448145081686846">YES! DAT ENDING DOE.<br/><br/>Okay, I was totally prepared to give this, like, 3.5 or 4 stars. It was enjoyable, but there wasn't much going on storywise. And then somewhere nearing the end things went exactly in the direction I wanted it to go, and the ending--even though it's a cliffhanger--still left me really really fucking satisfied. I thought this book was good before, but after finishing it, I can honestly say I would stamp "AWESOME" onto the cover.<br/><br/>Also, side note; before I read this book, I joking</span>
  <span id="freeText16651448145081686846" style="display:none">YES! DAT ENDING DOE.<br /><br />Okay, I was totally prepared to give this, like, 3.5 or 4 stars. It was enjoyable, but there wasn't much going on storywise. And then somewhere nearing the end things went exactly in the direction I wanted it to go, and the ending--even though it's a cliffhanger--still left me really really fucking satisfied. I thought this book was good before, but after finishing it, I can honestly say I would stamp "AWESOME" onto the cover.<br /><br />Also, side note; before I read this book, I jokingly put in this review that perhaps Ivy was a descendant of Chaolaena (Celaena and Chaol from the <i>Throne of Glass</i> series) since her last name is Westfall. Do I still think it? Sure, why not? xD Ivy wasn't as badass as Celaena, but she was still pretty likable, and I have a feeling she <i>will</i> be more badass in book 2.<br /><br />Lots of fun, this was! Really satisfying ending. I has high hopes for the rest of the series.</span>

    <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus"><img alt="April (Aprilius Maximus)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589331862p2/20658145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089134193?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April (Aprilius Maximus)" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus">April (Aprilius Maximus)</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089134193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18257267130873758233">EXCUSE ME WHILE I PICK UP THE PIECES OF MY HEART THAT JUST SHATTERED ALL OVER THE PLACE</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1442642870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1442642870" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1442642870?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=strong-emotions">strong-emotions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=realism">realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=will-reread">will-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=highly-recommend">highly-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=beautiful-stories">beautiful-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=light-read">light-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=ebooks-ibooks">ebooks-ibooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1442642870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12152246867209627008"> <b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"A boy who doesn't want to lie, married to a girl who can't tell the truth."</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>The moment I saw this stunning cover, I've made up my mind whatever happened, I'll read it. Because, c'mon! Isn't it eye-catching?<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454854184i/18022463.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>-Her white backless dress indicated her early wedding.<br/>-The knife held behind her back meant the very purpose she needed to get close to him.<br/>-The silhouette of the city resembled where the story took place, including Westfall(West) and Lattimer(East) sides of it.<br/><br/>This is a story abo</span>
  <span id="freeText12152246867209627008" style="display:none"> <b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"A boy who doesn't want to lie, married to a girl who can't tell the truth."</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br>The moment I saw this stunning cover, I've made up my mind whatever happened, I'll read it. Because, c'mon! Isn't it eye-catching?<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454854184i/18022463.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>-Her white backless dress indicated her early wedding.<br>-The knife held behind her back meant the very purpose she needed to get close to him.<br>-The silhouette of the city resembled where the story took place, including Westfall(West) and Lattimer(East) sides of it.<br><br>This is a story about <i>arranged marriage.</i> Following our beloved female mc, <b>Ivy Westfall</b>, she was forced to marry some guy she never met before her marriage when she was 16. Previously reminder: Long before the war in the U.S., the <i>Westfall</i> and the <i>Lattimer</i> family had been enemy politically; the former was the founder of the place, yet was under full control of the latter. With the view of seeking peace between the two parties, Lattimer legitimated the arranged marriage for boys and girls from both sides of the city to marry each other. Since Ivy's father was supposed to be the President instead of Mr. Lattimer, she served as a spy and had an important mission when she married <b>Bishop Lattimer</b>, the only son of President Lattimer. <br><br>In the beginning, she thought it would be easy to accomplish her goal, but as time went by, she realized that he wasn't what her father and older sister, <b>Callie</b>, had prepared her for. He wasn't the guy they thought would abuse her like some unfortunate, typical arranged marriages. Better yet, he appeared to have a kind heart and his words were genuine enough to send warmth to her. <b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>When his scream fades into silence, he rests his forehead against the metal. "Sometimes," he says, voice raw, "I hate this place." He twists his neck and looks at me, hands still hooked in the fence above his head.<br>"I know," I say, barely a whisper. "Me, too." </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>However, with her constant meeting with Callie, her sister kept reminding her how crucial Ivy's phase of the entire plan was and stopped her from chickening out. So Ivy was caught in a dilemma, whether she had to choose a boy who helped her find freedom and the way to save herself, or someone who shared the same blood. <b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>You're easy to read, Ivy, but the whole book of you is complicated.</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><b>I love the plot a lot, but somehow there's something missing in it.</b> The chapters are pretty short and light to read; the action is addictive and really fast-paced, though I think if there are more tension and interaction between the <i>newly-wed</i>, it will undoubtedly make this story so much captivating and complete. Not that I'm complaining, it's just that I prefer more twists and pages and chapters for such a fantastic page-turner. Honestly, I just can't get enough of Ivy &amp; Bishop! Bishop is definitely the best role model for an ideal boyfriend; he possessed all kinds of quality I'm expecting a bf has. He was extremely considerate and could always put himself into others' shoes or knew Ivy well despite the fact that she wasn't good at telling the truth of all time. In a nutshell, he knew how to sweet talk and still express himself truthfully. It's hard not to melt under the influence of his cheesy words. <b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"Why me?" I ask.<br>"Because everyone needs someone to put their faith in," Bishop says. "Life's too lonely otherwise. And I'm putting mine in you."</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br>The ending was rather heartbreaking. It's amazing how such a short story could still strongly make me emotional. I'm not easy to cry over a book, but this one got me. Perhaps some may consider the end too cliche but for me, I just loved it. As a result, I can't wait to see how she dealt with her <i>Poison Ivy</i> behavior and the severe consequence she was responsible for.<br><br>Last but not least, I totally <b>recommend</b> this book/duology to everyone. It's a very enjoyably light read to get pass reading slumps and also a beautiful love story for someone who were forced to marry strangers. <b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Love isn't something you can legislate. Love is more than charts and graphs and matching interests. Love is messy and complicated and it is a mistake to deny its random magic.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12152246867209627008" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1315237198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1315237198" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1315237198?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=listened-on-audio">listened-on-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1315237198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6852739857978696356"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Lately, I have been a bit weary of hype. Hype can be a great thing because it enables you to find books you would otherwise never have picked up. However, it can also take the fun out of reading because you practically already know everything about a book before you’ve even read the first page. This is why I decided to pick up The Book of Ivy, which I really hadn’t heard that much about previously. In this case, the decision paid of. I really enjoyed this novel; it was a very short, qui</span>
  <span id="freeText6852739857978696356" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />Lately, I have been a bit weary of hype. Hype can be a great thing because it enables you to find books you would otherwise never have picked up. However, it can also take the fun out of reading because you practically already know everything about a book before you’ve even read the first page. This is why I decided to pick up The Book of Ivy, which I really hadn’t heard that much about previously. In this case, the decision paid of. I really enjoyed this novel; it was a very short, quick read.<br /><br />The Book of Ivy is a dystopian novel that takes place in the future after the United States has been destroyed by a nuclear war. Most people were completely wiped out and there was only a small population left. These people came together to establish a new “nation” but there were two rival sides: the Westfalls and the Lattimers. The Lattimers won and now, fifty years later, peace and control is maintained by marrying the daughters of the losing side to the sons of the winning group. <br />The story follows Ivy Westfall, who is forced to marry Bishop Lattimer at the age of sixteen. What nobody outside of Ivy’s family knows however, is that Ivy is on a mission to kill Bishop in order to restore the Westfall family to power. <br /><br />My feelings for this book are bit all over the place so let’s break it down, shall we?<br /><br /><u>World building:</u><br /><br />The world building is definitely the weakest part of the novel. It was <b>meager at best</b>. We got practically no explanations for what happened to the world. Although politics are the central issue in the novel, they were very simplified and not exploited. Having said that though, I was <b>surprised by how little I actually cared about the lack of world building</b>. This is very unusual for me, as I am world building freak; it’s part of why I love fantasy so much. Somehow, I found myself enjoying the story and not dwelling too much on the fact that nothing was really explained.<br /><br /><u>Characters:</u><br /><br />I mostly really enjoyed the main characters, even though I did have a few problems with both of them.<br /><br /><b>Ivy was a very relatable and likeable protagonist. She is very compassionate and outspoken yet also impulsive which gets her into trouble.</b> At times I did find Ivy a tad annoying, simply because she kept repeating the same thoughts over and over again in her head and her impulsiveness seemed quite <b>reckless</b>. Her character development was very typical for a dystopian: girl starts questioning and reevaluating her beliefs and realizes that some of the things she’s been taught her entire life are in fact incorrect or exaggerated. In that, she appeared a little indecisive and there were times where I just wanted to shake her. However, considering the fact that she was only sixteen and had been sheltered her entire life, she was a very <b>realistic character</b> and I found myself rooting for her. <b>I could really feel how torn she was between the loyalty to her family and her budding feelings towards Bishop.</b> <br /><br />In my opinion (and I’m sure some of you will agree with me) there is a big difference between the bookish boyfriends we love to swoon over in our favorite books and the ones we would actually like to date in real life. Many brooding, dark bad boys might be amazing to read about, but if they were real I would probably steer clear. Bishop, however, is the opposite. He is literally <b>the PERFECT guy in every way</b>, everything anyone could ever want in a boyfriend. <b>He is very kind and handsome, trusting and considerate, intelligent and selfless.</b> <br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I want to be someone strong and brave enough to make hard choices. But I want to be fair and loving enough to make the right ones."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />And that’s where the problem lies: as much as I loved Bishop, I don’t like characters that don’t have flaws. Not just out of principle, but because they are kind of…bland, dull. <b>He was adorable but not interesting.</b> <br /><br /><u>Plot &amp; Romance:</u><br /><br />The book of Ivy is essentially a <b>love story</b>. Yes, there are political and ideological elements involved but at its core it’s a novel about two star-crossed lovers. The plot wasn’t particularly thrilling but it did keep my attention throughout and the ending was very unexpected. I’m definitely curious to know what happens in the second installment since it’s going to have a very different premise than the first one!<br /><br />I really enjoyed the romance, it was <b>very cute and there was no insta-love or love triangle</b>. Hallelujah! Some readers might consider their relationship too sweet (I sure thought I would) but honestly, I found myself <b>completely engaged</b>. The one thing I didn’t like was that cliché towards the end <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Bishop telling Ivy he wanted to meet her from the first time her saw her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, which made me question what exactly Bishop saw in Ivy. <br /><br /><u>Themes &amp; Writing:</u><br /><br /><b>This book does attempt to make people think.</b> It asks some difficult questions with no right or wrong answers. Which side should Ivy chose? What is the morally correct thing to do? Can there be a positive outcome?<br />I also appreciated that the novel <b>explored sexism and the role of women in society.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I'm not sure how we got to this place, where a girl's only value is in what kind of marriage she has, how capable she is of keeping a man happy.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />It’s still an issue and an important thing to talk about.<br /><br />The writing was very simple yet gripping and fluid. Nothing special but definitely serviceable. <br /><br /><u>Overall:</u><br /><br />I really enjoyed The Book of Ivy but it didn’t blow me away. <b>It’s not a very original story, nothing I haven’t read before, however, the execution is well done and it was a very quick and engaging read.</b> I recommend it if you like dystopians with a heavy emphasis on romance. I will be picking up book two.<br /><br />This review can also be found on <a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Geek</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6852739857978696356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5323810273254156117">THIS BOOK WAS AMAZING!!!!<br/><br/>You guys, you NEED to read this! I couldn't put it down! I read it in 2 sittings which never happens!   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1437533307" />
    <a title="Shannon (kitchandpages)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10961933-shannon-kitchandpages"><img alt="Shannon (kitchandpages)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441470068p2/10961933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1437533307?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon (kitchandpages)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon (kitchandpages)" href="/user/show/10961933-shannon-kitchandpages">Shannon (kitchandpages)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1437533307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8124086990467328777">My thoughts on The Book of Ivy are quite simple: I loved it.<br/><br/>It's been awhile since I have picked up a straight young adult dystopian book and I have to say that the experience was refreshing. This book is a testament to the idea that less can be WAY more. There is nothing complicated or overly complex about the book and honestly, it is part of what made is so enjoyable.<br/><br/>Amy Engel was able to capture something familiar yet enticing with her balance between politics and romance. The Book of Ivy, at</span>
  <span id="freeText8124086990467328777" style="display:none">My thoughts on The Book of Ivy are quite simple: I loved it.<br /><br />It's been awhile since I have picked up a straight young adult dystopian book and I have to say that the experience was refreshing. This book is a testament to the idea that less can be WAY more. There is nothing complicated or overly complex about the book and honestly, it is part of what made is so enjoyable.<br /><br />Amy Engel was able to capture something familiar yet enticing with her balance between politics and romance. The Book of Ivy, at it's core, is a romance between two teens on the opposite sides of a political war. You have Ivy, who is the daughter of a gilted would-be leader, who is determined to bring his family back to power. Then there is Bishop, the privileged and seemingly spoiled son of the president of Westfall, Mr. Lattimer. But there is a lot more to both teens story than meets the eye.<br /><br />So on the joining of their families through their arranged marriage, we see them in a new position, away from both influences and forced to face the truth that both families may have lied and that they might not be what the other was expecting.<br /><br />I found the romance in this book SO ADDICTING. It was a slow burn that had me turning pages, unable to put it down. I HAD to know what happened next between Ivy and Bishop and just when I thought I knew what would happen, I would be thrown off-guard.<br /><br />It's a fast-paced read that will have you begging for more. And that ending?! SO CRAZY.<br /><br />4.5 stars<br /><br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://leaninglights.blogspot.com/">http://leaninglights.blogspot.com/</a></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1103397515" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103397515" />
    <a title="Paula M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23287093-paula-m"><img alt="Paula M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601006204p2/23287093.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23287093-paula-m?shelf=all-them-feels">all-them-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23287093-paula-m?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23287093-paula-m?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23287093-paula-m?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1103397515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7270082245326456009">You can also read my review <a href='http://herbookthoughts.reads-it.com/?p=1803' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE.</a><br/><br/> <strong><em><blockquote>"My mission is not to make him happy and bear his children and be his wife. My mission is to kill him"</blockquote></em></strong><br/><br/> Never mind that I have to wait for a year to read the sequel.<br/><br/><a href='http://herbookthoughts.reads-it.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/wpid-aon_idontcare_iloveit.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'><img alt='image' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415881340ra/11858945.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a> <br/><br/><br/>This book! This awesome and fantastic and brilliant book kept me up all night an I'm not even complaining! I remember saying ‘Okay, just the first chapter' then BAM! After almost 5 hours, I'm still in the same position, I've forgotten my hunger and bladder and yes, I was bit of a mess. <strong>Amy Engel, you</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText7270082245326456009" style="display:none">You can also read my review <a href="http://herbookthoughts.reads-it.com/?p=1803" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE.</a><br><br> <strong><em><blockquote>"My mission is not to make him happy and bear his children and be his wife. My mission is to kill him"</blockquote></em></strong><br><br> Never mind that I have to wait for a year to read the sequel.<br><br><a href="http://herbookthoughts.reads-it.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/wpid-aon_idontcare_iloveit.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img alt="image" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415881340ra/11858945.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <br><br><br>This book! This awesome and fantastic and brilliant book kept me up all night an I'm not even complaining! I remember saying ‘Okay, just the first chapter' then BAM! After almost 5 hours, I'm still in the same position, I've forgotten my hunger and bladder and yes, I was bit of a mess. <strong>Amy Engel, you are one genius lady!</strong><br><br> Ivy is the daughter of the founder (the losing side) of their community, and as a tradition, she's part of the many teenagers who must marry the boys of the group who won to maintain peace. Because Ivy is special, the guy she's marrying is pretty special too. Its none other than the son's president, Bishop. Ivy doesn't care all about that because she only have one mission. And that's to kill Bishop, which should be easy because even before they met, she already hated him for his fathers doing. <strong>But Bishop turned out to be different from what Ivy is expecting, which made things complicated.</strong><br><br> Ooooooh man. <strong>The characterization in this book is superb.</strong> Ivy is a very likeable protagonist. She may seem cold and distant at the first chapter, but as soon as she starts revealing the plans that she and her family planned, I started enjoying her POV's more. I felt for her. I can really feel how torn she is between her loyalty to her family to the guy she's starting to love. Talk about decisions!!<br><br> <strong>The plot was intense and absolutely thrilling.</strong> The author knows how to grip her readers. She knows when to make her readers gasps, or when to melt them with one of Bishop's line or when to break their hearts from Ivy's monologue. Seriously. <u><strong>For a debut novel, this is impressive. </strong></u><br><br> What I really love about The Book of Ivy is that <strong>it will make you think.</strong> Morally, politically and you'll find yourself asking if what would you do if you're in Ivy's shoes. What is the right thing to do? Who has the right to say that its right.. or that its wrong. And who's side is the right one?<br><br> World building needs more improvement but for the first book, its very believable and convincing. <strong>The Book of Ivy has well written characters, gripping writing and heartfelt romance. Throw in some lies, twists and surprises... you have that successful dystopia book you're looking for.</strong> <u>One of my favorite this year!</u></span>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1419527966?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate (GirlReading)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate (GirlReading)" href="/user/show/29599654-kate-girlreading">Kate (GirlReading)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1419527966" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4462939345636947268">4.5* <br/><br/>With politics, assassination plots, secrets and romance, The Book of Ivy is without a doubt one of the most enjoyable dystopians I have read in years. <br/><br/>I had no idea what to expect going in to this but I definitely don't expect to love it so much. It had me totally engrossed from the first page until the last. I adored the characters, (Bishop officially has a place in my heart) and the relationship dynamics were addictive and layered. I absolutely fell in love with the romance. Oh the romanc</span>
  <span id="freeText4462939345636947268" style="display:none">4.5* <br /><br />With politics, assassination plots, secrets and romance, The Book of Ivy is without a doubt one of the most enjoyable dystopians I have read in years. <br /><br />I had no idea what to expect going in to this but I definitely don't expect to love it so much. It had me totally engrossed from the first page until the last. I adored the characters, (Bishop officially has a place in my heart) and the relationship dynamics were addictive and layered. I absolutely fell in love with the romance. Oh the romance. It was gorgeously addictive, heartbreaking and eurgh, just played with my heart in all the right ways. The fast paced plot had my full attention throughout and I honestly can't remember enjoying a dystopian quite as much as this since The Hunger Games years. It was addictive, gritty, heart pounding and impossible to put down. <br /><br />TW: Rape. Suicide.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1140207987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7550916013574278934">Review also available at:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress.com/2017/10/13/the-book-of-ivy-amy-engel/#more-4573'>https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress....</a><br/><br/>This book, especially the ending, gave me feels. The author did a really good job here of developing her characters, building her plot and writing in a beautiful, suspenseful style.<br/><br/>Let me start with Ivy, she was a really well thought out character whom I could emphasise with throughout the book (even though the way she never ratted on her family frustrated me). She was constantly under pressure from society and her family to perfor</span>
  <span id="freeText7550916013574278934" style="display:none">Review also available at:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress.com/2017/10/13/the-book-of-ivy-amy-engel/#more-4573">https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress....</a><br /><br />This book, especially the ending, gave me feels. The author did a really good job here of developing her characters, building her plot and writing in a beautiful, suspenseful style.<br /><br />Let me start with Ivy, she was a really well thought out character whom I could emphasise with throughout the book (even though the way she never ratted on her family frustrated me). She was constantly under pressure from society and her family to perform in different ways, but the way her romance with Bishop developed was to me, heartwarming and well crafted. Bishop himself was also a strong well-developed character with a lot of depth and personality to him and I would definitely say he has just as much potential as Ivy in the next book.<br /><br />At the beginning there was some sort of world history, but for me I think it could have been a tad more in-depth with more about how the war developed and more on how the two families formed. But other than that it really did set up the scene well and the world was very believable.<br /><br />The writing. Oh yes, I loved the way this author writes and while this wasn’t an action driven plot, the writing itself still managed to make the story exciting. Engel also manages to play with our feelings throughout as myself and a lot of others on GR were saying the ending was crazy and for me in particular it was a rollercoaster of feels.<br /><br />So this was a very exciting and thoughtful ride with lots going on and an easy reading style. (In fact I loved that ending so much that I immediately ordered the next book from my library as soon as I’d turned the last page!)</span>

<div id="review_1059734571" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1059734571" />
    <a title="Anatea Oroz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4183325-anatea-oroz"><img alt="Anatea Oroz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545147569p2/4183325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1059734571?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anatea Oroz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anatea Oroz" href="/user/show/4183325-anatea-oroz">Anatea Oroz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4183325-anatea-oroz?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4183325-anatea-oroz?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4183325-anatea-oroz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4183325-anatea-oroz?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1059734571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11345839015518681"><b>
  <a href='http://anateasbookshelf.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This review is also posted on my blog, Anatea's Bookshelf.</a>
</b><br/><br/>Every time I see a dystopia book, I'm kind of skeptic to read it because they all have so similar concept and I can't help but feel that I've already read something alike. I'm happy to say that it wasn't the case with The Book of Ivy. I was actually pleasantly surprised with its concept and its originality, even though it had some dystopia stereotypes. I ended up LOVING the book! Though, I think that a lot of my doubts were because of</span>
  <span id="freeText11345839015518681" style="display:none"><b>
  <a href="http://anateasbookshelf.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">This review is also posted on my blog, Anatea's Bookshelf.</a>
</b><br /><br />Every time I see a dystopia book, I'm kind of skeptic to read it because they all have so similar concept and I can't help but feel that I've already read something alike. I'm happy to say that it wasn't the case with The Book of Ivy. I was actually pleasantly surprised with its concept and its originality, even though it had some dystopia stereotypes. I ended up LOVING the book! Though, I think that a lot of my doubts were because of the cover. I know I shouldn't judge a book by its cover, but I can't help it. It's the first thing I notice about the book, and this cover just isn't something that would make me want to read the book. Entangled people, please re-design this cover and make a better one that would do the book justice. <br /><br />After a nuclear war, two families, Westfall and Lattimer, ended up fighting for the power. Lattimer's were the winners, while the Westfall's lost. To ensure the peace between the two sides of the country, they decided to arrange marriages for their children. All girls from the losing side should marry a guy from the winning side, and the girls from winning side should marry a guy from losing side. This year it is time for Ivy Westfall to marry, and none other but the son of the president, Bishop Lattimer. Unhappy with the Lattimer's rule, Westfall's conspire to dethrone Lattimer's, and Ivy has an important task in the mission. To kill Bishop Lattimore, her future husband. But is her family right? And, will she be able to do it?<br /><br />Ivy was the kind of character who I was wary about at first, but as the book went on, I slowly began to like her. At first, she seemed cold and like she had no brain of her own. She was following whatever her family said to her and never questioned it, but later, when she married Bishop and started to see that not everything her family tells her is true, she started to question their intentions, she started thinking about it, and it's her sense of morality that made me like her in the end. <br /><br /><blockquote>"It's doubtly important that we think for ourselves. We're not our parents. We don't have to agree with everything they stand for."</blockquote><br /><br />It's completely different story with Bishop. I fell in love with him straight away. I could see that he would be a good guy and I was praying Ivy would notice it too. I loved how they slowly built their friendship and trust in each other. I loved how invested Bishop was in knowing Ivy, and I loved how their romance progressed. It was the right kind of slow-burning romance. <br /><br /><blockquote>"If I had to get married, I wanted to marry someone who I was interested in knowing. You're easy to read, Ivy, but the whole book of you is complicated. That's why I wanted you instead of your sister."</blockquote><br /><br />For the end, the only thing I have left to say is that you will not regret reading The Book of Ivy. Even if you're not a fan of dystopia books, I'm sure you'll fall in love with this amazing book and it'll make you flip the pages so fast you won't even notice that you read the whole thing in one go. But beware, after that ending, you'll wish the next one to come out right away!<br /><br /><b><a href="http://anateasbookshelf.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/anateaoroz" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/AnateasAdventures" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://instagram.com/anateaoroz/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/anateaoroz/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11345839015518681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15851662810986534022" style="display:none">This book was so addicting! I had to stay up until 3:30AM to finish it because I had to know what happened. Bishop may also be my new book boyfriend. ;) All silliness aside this book was dark and provided an interesting perspective on women's rights and a society without democracy, and had me feeling very grateful for my own life. While the beginning of the book was a bit predictable, the ending certainly was not. I want the next book, but I've heard mixed things. We'll see...I don't think I can go without knowing what happens to Ivy and Bishop.</span>

<div id="review_1060508095" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1060508095" />
    <a title="Rebekah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2669249-rebekah"><img alt="Rebekah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554772145p2/2669249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1060508095?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebekah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebekah" href="/user/show/2669249-rebekah">Rebekah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669249-rebekah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669249-rebekah?shelf=ya-addiction">ya-addiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1060508095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer928344800259220667">Original Review at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com'>www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>What a GREAT book! I knew I wanted to read it but wasn't sure how I would enjoy it. Let me tell you how much I loved this book...I started it at 8:30ish in the evening and didn't put it down till after 2 in the freaking morning! AHHHH so good, in fact so good that I tweeted the author telling her how upset I am that I have to WAIT for book 2! GAH!<br/><br/>This book is engaging, entertaining, unputdownable, sweet, exciting, and devastating!<br/><br/>The story foll</span>
  <span id="freeText928344800259220667" style="display:none">Original Review at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com">www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com</a><br><br>What a GREAT book! I knew I wanted to read it but wasn't sure how I would enjoy it. Let me tell you how much I loved this book...I started it at 8:30ish in the evening and didn't put it down till after 2 in the freaking morning! AHHHH so good, in fact so good that I tweeted the author telling her how upset I am that I have to WAIT for book 2! GAH!<br><br>This book is engaging, entertaining, unputdownable, sweet, exciting, and devastating!<br><br>The story follows a society where 2 parties went to war, 1 party fell and the other party's family rose in power. To keep the peace between the 2 fighting parties/families the daughter, (Ivy Westfall) would marry the son of the President (Bishop Lattimer).<br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-gRsmDdflXEQ/VIMs5XDQiJI/AAAAAAAAFdU/rDxULiQrZPs/s1600/tumblr_lzjjc0lSAQ1qij4o1o1_1280.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419780411i/13125054._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br>I loved Ivy's character because she was so human and so relatable. This girl who was raised by the family who fell and who knew her sister would marry the son of the President in order to kill him so their revolution may commence so justice and the rights and order be brought back to where it "belonged." But when Bishop lets everyone know that he will not marry till he is 18 that pushes Ivy's sister out of the league to marry and kill him, so when Ivy becomes the next in line to marry Bishop she is rushed into training and everything in order to do what she needs to do to carry out her father's wishes and kill Bishop.<br>I loved that she was so human with the desire to do what is right, please her family, question everything that she was taught to believe, she has fears, she finds the truth behind the lies and learns to sacrifice when the time comes.<br><br>Enjoyed her character development, I thought it was just the right amount of time and essence to get the reader invested in this character.<br><div>
<br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-1NfzV_CGMJc/VIMuX-qArKI/AAAAAAAAFdc/y3LtGvPsXhE/s1600/e0742422775f392ca331b137dfad8fbc.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419780411i/13125055._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>I also loved how the author chose to write Bishop Lattimer's character. I feel that in a lot of YA authors are writing in "bad boys" that treat girls not nicely and still have the female girls fall in love with them and somehow the "bad boy" changes and is all works out? I mean really what is that setting girls up for? but that is another topic.<br><br>Bishop is NOT what Ivy was taught to believe he is. He is everything a man should be, he is kind, gentle, thoughtful, aware, helpful, hard working, and everything that makes this male character "swoon worthy."<br><br>Overall I loved the story and look forward to book 2!<br><br>Sexual Content: mild (PG-some talk of honeymoon night)<br>Language: mild<br>Violence: moderate (talk of killing, of a hanging, a woman getting hit)<br>Drugs/Alcohol: mild</div></span>
  <a data-text-id="928344800259220667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1433181386" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1433181386" />
    <a title="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog"><img alt="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576986930p2/28353412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1433181386?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" href="/user/show/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog">Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23265889-the-book-of-ivy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=insta-not-used">insta-not-used</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=good-boys-i-love">good-boys-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=romance-forbidden-or-starcrossed">romance-forbidden-or-starcrossed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=yessss-sexual-tension">yessss-sexual-tension</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1433181386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11756818845626503335"><b>***4.5/5 Stars***</b><br/><blockquote>
  
    <b>Our story was written long ago, and it does not have a happy ending.</b>
  
</blockquote><br/><b>The Book of Ivy was so much fun, and I quickly devoured it in two sittings!</b> It's just one of those books that you can step right into and easily enjoy it from the first page on. The characters, the world building, the way the story progressed, it was all so effortless to connect with. And yes, I'm definitely kicking myself for not picking up this book sooner!<br/><blockquote>
  
    <b>Once I’m safely out of range, I re</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText11756818845626503335" style="display:none"><b>***4.5/5 Stars***</b><br><blockquote>
  
    <b>Our story was written long ago, and it does not have a happy ending.</b>
  
</blockquote><br><b>The Book of Ivy was so much fun, and I quickly devoured it in two sittings!</b> It's just one of those books that you can step right into and easily enjoy it from the first page on. The characters, the world building, the way the story progressed, it was all so effortless to connect with. And yes, I'm definitely kicking myself for not picking up this book sooner!<br><blockquote>
  
    <b>Once I’m safely out of range, I realize this is the first time I’ve spent more than five minutes with him where I wasn’t thinking about the plan or what to do next. Which is exactly what my father and Callie want, for me to act natural, to make it seem real. I should be happy. But I remember Bishop’s laugh, his crinkly nose, the warmth in my cheeks, and can’t help feeling I’ve done something wrong.</b>
  
</blockquote><br>The story starts off with us following Ivy, who is on her way to get married to a stranger. And that stranger is the President's son, Bishop. Yet<b> Ivy isn't looking forward to a happily ever after with her new husband. Instead, she is looking forward to helping out her family's agenda, which involves murdering her new husband-to-be so her family can step back into power.</b> And in the beginning, I was all for that plan. I hated how the President maintained their population by arranged marriage. That at the age of 16-18 they were expected to get married and for the women to start popping out babies. I understood the importance of keeping up their population of 10,000, since the U.S. had been decimated from war, floods, drought, famine etc. But I also understood the importance of Ivy's family taking back the power and changing the marriage laws along with a slew of other things. So<b> I was on board with Ivy murdering the President's son, but then I met Bishop.</b><br><blockquote>
  
    <b>“Sometimes,” he says, voice raw, “I hate this place.” He twists his neck and looks at me, hands still hooked in the fence above his head.<br> “I know,” I say, barely a whisper. “Me, too.”</b>
  
</blockquote><br><b>Leave it up to me to fall for the man who is supposed to get murdered. I couldn't help it, but I loved Bishop!</b> From the moment he squeezed her hand before the wedding ceremony, I was a goner. Yup, I'm that easy lol. If you follow my reviews, you know I'm one of those people who always looks for the tiniest of clues to show that someone is worthy of falling for. And <b>Bishop gave me so much hope. He was thoughtful, compassionate, caring and was open with her at times. And his actions and words slowly started to plant foreign thoughts in her head and mine. Who could we trust? Was Bishop being honest or was he tricking Ivy</b>? I struggled trying to figure out Bishop's motives, but I definitely didn't struggle falling head over heels in love with every single tiny beautiful thing Bishop did.<br><blockquote>
  
    <b>My head knows what a horrible idea this is, screaming at me to </b>
    <b>
      <i>stop,</i>
    </b>
    <b> that I’m taking things too far, but the rest of me has no such reservations. I have the fleeting thought that perhaps self-preservation isn’t my strongest character trait.</b>
  
</blockquote><br>Bishop and Ivy slowly started to get to know each other, after they were married. It wasn't always smooth, and they definitely had their share of fights. But <b>underneath their fights and their uncertainty around each other was always something simmering. They had the best slow burn romance that continued to burn hotter and hotter as each moment passed. </b>It was undeniable. So regardless of whether they were making each other smile, or making each other's blood boil, there was always that sexual tension. And it was so, so, so good!<br><blockquote>
  
    <b>I’ve learned the hard way, we can’t choose who we love. Love chooses us. Love doesn’t care about what’s convenient or easy or planned. Love has its own agenda and all we can do is get out of its way.</b>
  
</blockquote><br>While I guessed how a few things would go, one thing went in an entirely different direction than I thought it would! But that's probably because I didn't always agree with Ivy's decisions. There were things I wanted her to say and do, or not do, yet she had her own agenda and her own plans. So<b> I'm nervously counting the seconds until I can pick up the final book and see how it all plays out. If you're looking for a Dystopian that is easy to get lost in and has a fabulous slow-burn romance, then I definitely recommend picking up The Book of Ivy!</b><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i> <br><a title="Star-Crossed Book Blog" href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287496i/17673736._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b> </b>
</u><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=on-my-real-shelves">on-my-real-shelves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=swoony-boys">swoony-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=true-5-starers">true-5-starers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=entangled">entangled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1055880082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16229167783163668932">Is there an “I’m in love with Bishop Lattimer” club? Because I need to be in it. <br/><br/>The Book of Ivy is probably going to be on my list of favorite books come the end of the year… and even though It’s only January I feel pretty confident in saying that. <br/><br/>It’s the future, and a brutal nuclear war has left what we think of as the United States barely unrecognizable. A group of survivors banded together to create their own town, but the families couldn’t agree on how to govern the people and war broke o</span>
  <span id="freeText16229167783163668932" style="display:none">Is there an “I’m in love with Bishop Lattimer” club? Because I need to be in it. <br /><br />The Book of Ivy is probably going to be on my list of favorite books come the end of the year… and even though It’s only January I feel pretty confident in saying that. <br /><br />It’s the future, and a brutal nuclear war has left what we think of as the United States barely unrecognizable. A group of survivors banded together to create their own town, but the families couldn’t agree on how to govern the people and war broke out between the two leaders. <br /><br />Years later, The Lattimer family has come out on the winning side and the Westfalls not so much. To maintain peace and control it’s determined that each year all the 16 year olds will be matched up to marry, so the losing sons and daughters are married off to the winning side hoping that will keep and kind of uprising from happening.<br /><br />This year Ivy Westfall turns 16 and she’s been specifically chosen to marry Bishop Lattimer, the President’s son. <br /><br />But Ivy has a task… she’s not just getting married, she’s finding a way in so that her family can end the Lattimers and take over control of the city. Ivy has been tasked with killing her husband.<br /><br />You guys… I started this book and I couldn’t put it down. <br /><br />I could sit here and tell you how amazing the writing is… because it is. I could tell you how wonderfully plotted the story is… because it is. I could tell you that Engel created this amazing post-apocalyptic world that is believable and a bit scary … because it is. Instead, I think I’d rather talk about Ivy and Bishop, our two main characters. <br /><br />Ivy, our sixteen year old heroine who has been forced into marriage with basically her family’s sworn enemy, has been waiting for the day that she could start proving to her family that she is strong, that she can fulfill the tasks that are necessary to restore them as leaders of the city. But what she doesn’t count on is Bishop himself. Ivy is smart and tough and fierce, but I think the characteristic I loved most about her was her empathy and her loyalty… and eventually her questioning all the things she was raised to believe about the Lattimer family and even her own beliefs about her family. <br /><br />And Bishop… good lord you guys. I heart him madly. He’s so not the boy that Ivy thought. He’s not just a sycophant of his father, he pushes Ivy to have her own thoughts and opinions and he listens to them even if he may not agree with them. <br /><br /><i>"I think," Bishop says, "that we can love our families without trusting everything they tell us. Without championing everything they stand for." He delivers the words matter-of-factly, but his eyes are locked on mine. "I think that sometimes things aren't as simple as our fathers want us to believe.” </i><br /><br />He’s kind to her and he’s sweet and patient and I’m pretty sure if you look up swoony in the dictionary you’ll find a picture of him there. <br /><br /><i>"Because I'm in love with you, Ivy," he whispers. "Giving up on you isn't an option." He lifts my hair away from the back of my neck and kisses the delicate skin there.<br />My breath shudders out of me. The silence spirals into the dark room, and maybe it was foolish to ask the question, but I'm not sorry. I uncurl his hand and kiss his palm, his skin cool and dry. I place his hand over my heart, cover it with my own.<br />We fall asleep that way. His lips on my neck. My heart in his hand.</i><br /> <br />I love that Engel took the time to let the relationship between them build and she let them get to know each other fully before any kind of romance was on the table… it made the story just that much more believable for me. <br /><br />The ending of this book will have you dying to get your hands on book 2 – I know I am. I can’t wait to see where Engel takes this story and what happens next! <br /><br />If you haven’t picked up The Book of Ivy then I highly recommend it. I’ll just be over here waiting for The Revolution of Ivy as patiently as possible! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16229167783163668932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1244698931" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1244698931" />
    <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway"><img alt="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456070558p2/32524334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1244698931?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway">Nina (Every Word A Doorway)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23265889-the-book-of-ivy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1244698931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer600706490456033915"><b>A light and quick read which does not strain too many brain cells</b>. This reminded me a lot of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10507293.The_Selection__The_Selection___1_' title='The Selection (The Selection, #1) by Kiera Cass' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Selection</a> – minus its painful main character, America Singer.<br/><br/>I read <i>The Book of Ivy</i> in one sitting. Despite its standard not being particularly high, I found my eyes glued to the pages, which brings to mind a term I’ve already used in my review for <i>The Selection</i>: <b>Addictive YA rubbish.</b><br/><br/>I’m going to keep this light and short like the book itself.<br/><br/><br/><u>The „rubbish“ part</u><br/><br/>☛ <b>The world-building was lacking.</b> There’</span>
  <span id="freeText600706490456033915" style="display:none"><b>A light and quick read which does not strain too many brain cells</b>. This reminded me a lot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10507293.The_Selection__The_Selection___1_" title="The Selection (The Selection, #1) by Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Selection</a> – minus its painful main character, America Singer.<br /><br />I read <i>The Book of Ivy</i> in one sitting. Despite its standard not being particularly high, I found my eyes glued to the pages, which brings to mind a term I’ve already used in my review for <i>The Selection</i>: <b>Addictive YA rubbish.</b><br /><br />I’m going to keep this light and short like the book itself.<br /><br /><br /><u>The „rubbish“ part</u><br /><br />☛ <b>The world-building was lacking.</b> There’s some info-dumping along the way about nuclear wars and survivors and power struggles, but the author keeps the world-building at a shallow level. <br /><br />☛ I thought most of the <b>characters were rather dull</b>, with the exception of the main character, Ivy Westfall. Let me describe the love interest, Bishop Lattimer: <b>Handsome, muscular, with perfect manners and idealistic visions.</b> In other words: too perfect. While I did enjoy Ivy’s interactions with Bishop, I was endlessly hoping for a spark of character – and I almost gave up on him, until he suddenly surprised me at the end. The <b>side characters were equally bland</b> and remained so throughout the book: Ivy’s family, Bishop’s family, and every other sorry soul that has crossed my path in this book. <br /><br />☛ The plot managed to keep me <b>entertained</b> (obviously) but it was rather <b>uneventful</b>, most of the ink being devoted to Ivy’s new life as Mrs. Lattimer. Meh.<br /><br /><br /><u>The „addictive“ part</u><br /><br />☛ <b>Ivy Westfall is one of the reasons this book earned 3 stars.</b> She’s engrossing with her quick-witted, loud mouth and her hunger for justice in her world. While she seems narrow-minded in the beginning, she soon begins to question her knowledge of right and wrong, seeing the world less in black ind white. I really liked this development. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>But I want to be better than the lessons they taught me. I want my love to be greater than my hate, my mercy to be stronger than my vengeance.</i>
</blockquote><br />In a world where arranged marriages are supposed to secure reproduction and the expansion of the almost eliminated human species, <b>Ivy continously finds herself questioning the anti-feministic system.</b> While the search for a match is more of a reality show in <i>The Selection</i>, it actually serves a greater purpose in <i>The Book of Ivy</i>. As the story progresses, Ivy also starts questioning her family, which leads to an <b>engrossing finale with a painful cliffhanger.</b> Damn you, Ivy, why must you have such shamelessly good morals? (Except for that moment where you lose it and almost rip someone to shreds with your bare hands… I salute you!). <br /><br />☛ The growing romance between Ivy and Bishop. <b>I’m a sucker for impossible or forbidden romance, so sue me.</b><br /><br /><br />Conclusively, if you’re looking for epic world-building, a range of engrossing characters and lush writing, you’ve got the wrong book. <b>What this book really has going for it is its heroine who does not fear to speak her mind, even if it gets her in trouble, and its entertainment level.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="600706490456033915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
